Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Notes to self:



<span class="line"><!---->Notes to self:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The issue is that the observer is being deleted but isn't being unregistered with the NetworkStateNotifier before that happens. So the next time the notifier goes to make a notification, it calls out to a deleted observer.



<span class="line"><!---->The issue is that the observer is being deleted but isn't being unregistered with the NetworkStateNotifier before that happens. So the next time the notifier goes to make a notification, it calls out to a deleted observer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So the question becomes, why isn't the unregister method being called? From tracking down the code, the Document has a Member<NetworkStateObserver>. The NetworkStateObserver has a std::unique_ptr<NetworkStateNotifier::NetworkStateObserverHandle>. The handle is a RAII object and will unregister the observer on destruction. So we need to make sure it gets destroyed before the NetworkStateObserver goes away. But that's not happening. I'm not very familiar with Oilpan but I'm guessing it's because the NetworkStateObserver's destructor isn't being called and so the unique_ptr for the handle isn't properly destroyed. Instead, it looks as if NetworkStateObserver is supposed to get a "ContextDestroyed" call from the ExecutionContextLifecycleObserver, but that's clearly not always happening. So, I guess I need to find a way to ensure that ContextDestroyed gets called. I have to say, I sure wish I could depend on RAII. Oilpan is complicated.



<span class="line"><!---->So the question becomes, why isn't the unregister method being called? From tracking down the code, the Document has a Member&lt;NetworkStateObserver&gt;. The NetworkStateObserver has a std::unique_ptr&lt;NetworkStateNotifier::NetworkStateObserverHandle&gt;. The handle is a RAII object and will unregister the observer on destruction. So we need to make sure it gets destroyed before the NetworkStateObserver goes away. But that's not happening. I'm not very familiar with Oilpan but I'm guessing it's because the NetworkStateObserver's destructor isn't being called and so the unique_ptr for the handle isn't properly destroyed. Instead, it looks as if NetworkStateObserver is supposed to get a "ContextDestroyed" call from the ExecutionContextLifecycleObserver, but that's clearly not always happening. So, I guess I need to find a way to ensure that ContextDestroyed gets called. I have to say, I sure wish I could depend on RAII. Oilpan is complicated.<!----></span>

Looking at the comment history in 



<span class="line"><!---->Looking at the comment history in <!----></span>





https://codereview.chromium.org/2714643008/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://codereview.chromium.org/2714643008/"><!---->https://codereview.chromium.org/2714643008/<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 it seems that this kind of issue isn't a big surprise. Reassigning to Kinuko as she understands the object lifetime model here much better than I do.



<span class="line"><!----> it seems that this kind of issue isn't a big surprise. Reassigning to Kinuko as she understands the object lifetime model here much better than I do.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Kinuko: There are cases in which NetworkStateObserver::ContextDestroyed isn't getting called before the observer is destroyed, and so the NetworkStateNotifier's raw pointer triggers a UAF. We could change the notifier to hold weakptrs, which is at least safer, but doesn't fix the underlying problem that we're not cleaning up our observer properly.



<span class="line"><!---->Kinuko: There are cases in which NetworkStateObserver::ContextDestroyed isn't getting called before the observer is destroyed, and so the NetworkStateNotifier's raw pointer triggers a UAF. We could change the notifier to hold weakptrs, which is at least safer, but doesn't fix the underlying problem that we're not cleaning up our observer properly.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I was able to prevent the problem in my local test by calling network_sate_observer_->ContextDestroyed() in Document::Shutdown() but I don't know if that's a good idea or not. 



<span class="line"><!---->I was able to prevent the problem in my local test by calling network_sate_observer_-&gt;ContextDestroyed() in Document::Shutdown() but I don't know if that's a good idea or not. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To reproduce, patch in the following code to periodically simulate switching from online/offline. If you let this run with asan for 20-30 seconds on the repro page given in the first post, it should trigger.

I don't know enough about the blink GC to say whether USING_PRE_FINALIZER is a good idea. Will USING_PRE_FINALIZER work if the owning class doesn't have a PRE_FINALIZER? What is the performance cost to a PRE_FINALIZER?



<span class="line"><!---->I don't know enough about the blink GC to say whether USING_PRE_FINALIZER is a good idea. Will USING_PRE_FINALIZER work if the owning class doesn't have a PRE_FINALIZER? What is the performance cost to a PRE_FINALIZER?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Adding haraken for guidance.



<span class="line"><!---->Adding haraken for guidance.<!----></span>

Can we call UnregisterAsObserver() when the ExecutionContext is detached (i.e., when ContextDestroyed is called)?



<span class="line"><!---->Can we call UnregisterAsObserver() when the ExecutionContext is detached (i.e., when ContextDestroyed is called)?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It's nice to clean up things in ContextDestroyed rather than a pre-finalizer. The timing of ContextDestroyed is well defined & most things are expected to stop on the execution context detachment. The timing of a pre-finalizer is GC-dependent.



<span class="line"><!---->It's nice to clean up things in ContextDestroyed rather than a pre-finalizer. The timing of ContextDestroyed is well defined &amp; most things are expected to stop on the execution context detachment. The timing of a pre-finalizer is GC-dependent.<!----></span>

Reg: ContextDestroyed and ExecutionContext sequence (rephrasing some of 



<span class="line"><!---->Reg: ContextDestroyed and ExecutionContext sequence (rephrasing some of <!----></span>





#c9



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c9"><!---->#c9<!----></a>





 and 



<span class="line"><!----> and <!----></span>





#c14



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c14"><!---->#c14<!----></a>





):



<span class="line"><!---->):<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





NetworkInformation implements ExecutionContextLifecycleObserver, and surely utilizes ContextDestroyed in order to determine if it needs to stop observing (and unregister the observers).  This also tries to avoid starting a new observer after ContextDestroyed is called, with a flag context_stopped_.



<span class="line"><!---->NetworkInformation implements ExecutionContextLifecycleObserver, and surely utilizes ContextDestroyed in order to determine if it needs to stop observing (and unregister the observers).  This also tries to avoid starting a new observer after ContextDestroyed is called, with a flag context_stopped_.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Relevant methods are:  NetworkInformation::ContextDestroyed(), NetworkInformation::{Start,Stop}Observing



<span class="line"><!---->Relevant methods are:  NetworkInformation::ContextDestroyed(), NetworkInformation::{Start,Stop}Observing<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So for regular sequences it looks it's doing the right thing.  One thing I wondered (which relates to the issue I hit in the fore-mentioned CL) is if the NetworkInformation might be created after the context is detached.  We check navigator.GetExecutionContext() before creating NetworkInformation in NetworkInformation::connection(), but don't check IsContextDestroyed() there.  I don't know if that's relevant in this case but if so we should avoid starting to observe (or even create a network information) if the context is already destroyed.



<span class="line"><!---->So for regular sequences it looks it's doing the right thing.  One thing I wondered (which relates to the issue I hit in the fore-mentioned CL) is if the NetworkInformation might be created after the context is detached.  We check navigator.GetExecutionContext() before creating NetworkInformation in NetworkInformation::connection(), but don't check IsContextDestroyed() there.  I don't know if that's relevant in this case but if so we should avoid starting to observe (or even create a network information) if the context is already destroyed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Looks like the newer RAII change is made by hajimehoshi@ in this CL, could you look into this one?



<span class="line"><!---->Looks like the newer RAII change is made by hajimehoshi@ in this CL, could you look into this one?<!----></span>



<br>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/722859/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/722859/"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/722859/<!----></a>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

the document.
